COMPACTION TESTING REPORT 
CAMPBELL HIGH SCHOOL NEW CLASSROOM BUILDING 
EWA, OAHU, HAWAII 
TMK No.: (1) 9-1-001: Parcel 002 
Grading Permit Nos. GP2018-02-0066 & GP2020-04-0157 
Dear Ms. Winchester: 
This report provides the compaction testing results performed during the site 
grading work for the Campbell High School New Classroom Building project from 
March 27, 2018 to January 22, 2019.  The compaction testing was performed by Hayre 
McElroy & Associates, LLC (HEAL) and Consolidated Engineering Laboratories (CEL). 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The project site is located within the James Campbell High School campus in the 
District of Ewa on the Island of Oahu, Hawaii.  The new building complex is located 
between the existing Library Building (Building “L”) on the east, and the existing Fine & 
Performing Arts Building (Building “J”) on the west. The new classroom complex will 
encompass approximately 53,000 square feet within a series of two- and three-story 
buildings.  The site grading involved cuts and fills of less than about 2 feet. A Project 
Location Map and Site Plan are shown on Plates 1 and 2, respectively.  
This report addresses the compaction testing performed during the site grading 
operations for the project site.  The compaction testing was performed by HEAL and CEL. 
COMPACTION TESTING  
The compaction testing was performed by HEAL and CEL at the above project site 
from March 27, 2018 to January 22, 2019.  The site grading work was performed by Koga 
Engineering and Construction, Inc.  During the site grading operations, samples of the 
on-site and imported fill materials were obtained for testing.  The maximum dry density and 
optimum moisture content were established in general accordance with ASTM Test 
Designation D1557 (Modified Proctor), and the test results are provided in the attached 
field reports. 
G70 
Page 2 
W.O. 7272-20 
October 19, 2020 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
The fill materials were moisture-conditioned to near optimum moisture content and 
compacted to a minimum of 90 or 95 percent of the maximum dry density as determined in 
accordance with ASTM Test Method D1557. 
During the site grading operations, periodic field density tests were performed in 
general accordance with ASTM Test Designation D2922 (Nuclear Gauge Method).  
Results of the compaction tests performed are provided in the attached field reports.  
These tests were performed on the prepared ground surfaces and on constructed fills at 
the site.   
Based on our review of HEAL and CEL’s field reports and compaction tests, it is our 
opinion that the compaction testing reviewed for the above-referenced project were in 
conformance with the general intent of the recommendations in the following references: 
1. 
Project Plans and Specifications. 
2. 
Report by Geolabs, Inc. entitled, “Geotechnical Engineering Exploration, 
New Classroom Building, James Campbell High School, Ewa, Oahu, 
Hawaii,” dated December 11, 2015. 
LIMITATIONS 
The compaction testing was performed by others and the compaction test results 
were reviewed by Geolabs for conformance to the project plans and specifications. The 
site grading work was not done under our observation.   
Provision of performing compaction testing is not insurance, nor does it guarantee 
construction of any type. The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the 
work, for adhering to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of 
when they are found.

density gauge.
Location: Fire Water main. Performed density tests on backfill previously compacted. Results attached.
Observed placement of material for remaining lifts. One area was slightly over moisture and was observed

Location: Temporary Parking. Performed density tests on native compacted material. Results attached.
Observed the placement of base course material.
Discussed observations and test results with Chris Cook of Swinerton.

Location and Description of Inspection
Task: Geotechnical Observation
Arrived onsite to observe the civil/site work performed by Koga and perform
compaction tests with nuclear density gauge.
Location: Fire Water main. Performed density tests for the top lift of native backfill
previously compacted. Results attached. | performed multiple tests in this area as
previous compaction attempts did not achieve relative density per spec.
Location: Temporary Parking. Performed density tests on base course
compacted material. Results attached. Initial attempts did not reach proper
relative density per spec. | observed recompaction of the area using a large
vibrating drum roller.
Discussed observations and test results with Chris Cook of Swinerton. The
pictures below show the area where work was performed.
Page 1 of 3
Fire water main backfill
Page 2 of 3
Temporary Parking Base Course
The proctor for the native material gives a value of 111.7 PCF with an optimum
moisture of 15.3%. The proctor for the base course gives a value of 128.6 PCF
with an optimum moisture of 9.8%.
All final tests taken and recorded today passed the project requirements for
relative compaction. To the best of my knowledge the material placed today was
done so per plans and project specifications.
Please see the Nuclear Density Form attached at the end of this report for the
detailed test results from today’s work.
Returned the Nuclear Density Gauge back to the Kapolei Lab.

Location and Description of Inspection
Task: Soils
Conducted Nuclear Density Testing at the following locations:
e Existing Fire lane backfill
Material backfilled into the area is native material. The proctor for the soil has an optimum dry
density of 111.7 PCF with optimum moisture of 15.9. The soils were moisture conditioned and
compacted by a jumping jack.
Took (3) test total, (3) which met or exceeded the project required 95% relative compaction.
Reported all results to the contractor as tests were performed to assure no confusion on whether
KOGA could move forward with backfilling and compaction or if re-work was required

Location and Description of Inspection
Task: Compaction Testing
A) Obtained the Nuclear Density Gauge from the Kapolei office.
B) Arrived on site and met with contractor. Performed a site walk of the area where work
will be performed today.
C) Crew on site placed and compacted multiple lifts for the interior backfill of footings at
building #4. A total of four lifts were placed, compacted, and tested for the culinary
area, and two lifts were placed, compacted, and tested for the kitchen area of building
#4. A tan sandy gravel with coral was used for backfill of this area. | performed multiple
tests on each lift in both the dining area and the kitchen area to ensure proper
compaction per spec. | also performed one test for footing F7 located roughly 20 feet
East of building #4. The pictures below show the area where work was performed.
Page 1 of 2
hayremcelroy -€
D) Compaction efforts of the material was via jumping jack and large roller. During
compaction efforts | took tests of the material with the Nuclear Density Gauge. Initial
tests were for QC purposes and if they were not passing of the project required 95%
relative density than | notified the contractor and they would continue rolling the area.
E) The proctor for the material used was provided by HMA which gives a value of 118.0
PCF with an optimum moisture of 13.4%.
F) All final tests taken and recorded today passed the project requirements for relative
compaction. To the best of my knowledge the material placed today was done so per
plans and project specifications.
G) Please see the Nuclear Density Form attached at the end of this report for the detailed
test results from today’s work.
H) Returned the Nuclear Density Gauge back to the Kapolei Lab.
Items Requiring Correction

Location and Description of Inspection
Task: Soil Compaction Testing
A) Conducted nuclear density testing at the following locations:
Various locations. Please see nuclear density form.
B) Material placed into this area was a tan coralline sand with gravel. The proctor for this material gives a MDD of 113.5
pcf and a optimum moisture of 13.1. | was onsite during the placement and compaction of this material. Electrical pad
and Building 4 back fill was compacted with a Vibratory Sheep foot roller and a jumping jack.
C) Conducted a total of 30 final tests, all of which met the projects required 95% relative compaction. Intermediary tests
used to monitor increased in compaction are not presented. Please see Nuclear Densometer Test Results at the end
of report. To the best of my knowledge, the material placed in this area was done so per plans and project
specifications.

Task: Compaction Testing
A) Obtained the Nuclear Density Gauge from the Kapolei office.
B) Arrived on site and met with contractor. Performed a site walk of the area where work
will be performed today.
C) Crew on site placed six lifts of material for the backfill of an old electrical trench where
an unused line was demo’d and removed. Trench was roughly five feet wide and 150
feet in length. A tan sandy gravel with coral was used for backfill of this area. |
performed multiple tests on each lift to ensure proper compaction per spec. The
pictures below show the area where work was performed.
Page 1 of 3
hayremcelroy -€-
D) Compaction efforts of the material was via large roller drum roller. During compaction
efforts | took tests of the material with the Nuclear Density Gauge. Initial tests were for
QC purposes and if they were not passing of the project required 90% relative density
than | notified the contractor and they would continue rolling the area.
E) The proctor for the material used was provided by HMA which gives a value of 118.0
PCF with an optimum moisture of 13.4%.
F) All final tests taken and recorded today passed the project requirements for relative
compaction. To the best of my knowledge the material placed today was done so per
plans and project specifications.
G) Please see the Nuclear Density Form attached at the end of this report for the detailed
test results from today’s work.
H) Returned the Nuclear Density Gauge back to the Kapolei Lab.
